باب ما يدعيه الرجلان
ماں کا شمن بخلاف کی قیمت اپنے بائع سے واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ بائع مشتری کے لئے مبیعہ باندی کی سلامتی کا ضامن تھا۔ عقر کے۔ کیونکہ یہ تو باندی کے منافع حاصل کرنے کی وجہ سے لازم ہوا ہے تو اس کو بائع سے واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ تشریح قوله ومن اشترى ... الخ - زید نے ایک باندی خریدی اس سے اس کے ایک بچہ ہوا اور زید نے اس کے نسب کا دعویٰ کیا۔ پھر وہ باندی کسی دوسرے کی نکل آئی تو باپ (یعنی زید ) بچہ کی قیمت کا تاوان دے گا اور قیمت میں خصومت کے دن کا اعتبار ہوگا اور بچہ آزاد ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ ولد المغر در ہے جو باجماع صحابہ اپنی قیمت سے آزاد ہوتا ہے۔ مغرور اس شخص کو کہتے ہیں جو ملک یمین یا ملک نکاح کے اعتماد پر کسی عورت سے صحبت کرے اور اس سے بچہ ہو جائے ۔ پھر وہ عورت کسی اور کی نکل آئے۔ قوله باجماع الصحابة .... الخ شیخ ابوبکر رازی نے شرح مختصر الطحاوی میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ صد راؤل اور فقہاء امصار میں اس کی بابت کوئی اختلاف نہیں کہ فریب خوردہ کا بچہ حر الاصل ہوتا ہے۔ اور اس بارے میں بھی کوئی اختلاف نہیں کہ وہ باپ پر مضمون ہوتا ہے۔ اختلاف صرف کیفیت ضمان کے بارے میں ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت عمر کا قول ہے۔ يفك الغلام بالغلام والجارية بالجارية يعنى ان كان الولد غلاماً فعلى الاب غلام مثله وان كان جاريةٌ فعليه جاريةٌ مثلها - حضرت على فرماتے ہیں کہ باپ پر بچہ کی قیمت واجب ہے۔ ہمارے اصحاب اسی طرف گئے ہیں اور حضرت عمر کے قول کی تاویل بھی یہی ہے ۔ يفك الغلام بقيمة الغلام
قوله ولان النظر من الجانبين. يہ عقلی دلیل ہے کہ مالک اتم اور بچہ کے باپ دونوں کا لحاظ رکھنا ضروری ہے۔ پس بچہ کے باپ کے لحاظ سے بچہ کو اصلی آزاداور مالک ام کے لحاظ سے رقیق قرار دیا جاتا ہے تا کہ جانئین کالحاظ ہو جائے۔ اور وہ یہی ہے کہ آزاد بعوض قیمت قرار دیا جائے پھر مذکورہ بچہ باپ کے قبضہ میں چونکہ بلا تعدی آیا ہے۔ تو وہ مستحق کے لئے ضامن صرف اس لئے ہے کہ وہ اس کو دینے سے روکتا ہے۔ جیسے مخصو بہ باندی کے بچہ میں ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا بچہ کی وہی قیمت معتبر ہوگی جو خصومت کے روز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اُسی دن روکا ہے۔ قوله ولومات الولد ... صورت مذکورہ میں اگر قبل از خصومت بچہ کا انتقال ہو جائے تو اس کے باپ پر کوئی تاوان نہ ہوگا بلکہ وہ صرف باندی مستحق کے حوالہ کرے گا۔ اس واسطے کہ اگر بچہ حقیقتا مستحق کا مملوک ہوتا تب وہ مضمون نہیں تھا تو ملک حقیقی نہ ہونے کی صورت میں بطریق اولی مضمون نہ ہوگا۔ نیز اگر اس بچہ کا کچھ تر کہ ہو تو اس کا وارث اس کا باپ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ باپ کے حق میں بچہ حراالاصل ہے۔ قوله ولو قتله الاب اگر اس بچہ کو باپ نے مارڈالا تو اس کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے روکنا پایا گیا۔ اسی طرح اگر اس کو کسی اور نے قتل کر دیا اور باپ نے اس کی قیمت کے بقدر اس کا خون بہا لے لیا۔ تو جیسے اس کی زندگی میں باپ نے تاوان دیا تھا۔ ایسے ہی اب بھی اس کا باپ مستحق کو بچہ کی قیمت کا تاوان دے گا۔ اور وہ بچہ کی قیمت اور اس کی ماں یعنی باندی کا شمن اپنے بائع سے وصول کر لے گا۔ کیونکہ بچہ اس باندی کا جز ہے اور باندی صبیح ہے۔ اور بائع مبیع کی سلامتی کا ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ تو عدم سلامتی مبیع کی صورت میں مشتری بائع سے وصول کرنے کا حقدار ہوگا۔ لیکن باندی کا جو عقر ( یعنی مہرشل ) مستحق کو دینا پڑاوہ نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ وہ تو منافع بضع حاصل کرنے کا بدل ہے۔ وعند الائمة الثلاثه يرجع بالعقر ايضا
Chapter: What two men claim. ... (The mother's price he will take back from his seller, because the seller was guarantor of the slave-girl's safety for the buyer. Except for the 'aqr, because that became obligatory due to deriving benefit from the slave-girl, so he cannot take that back from the seller. Commentary on his statement 'And whoever buys...': Zayd bought a slave-girl, she gave birth to a child, and Zayd claimed his lineage. Then the slave-girl turned out to belong to someone else. So the father (Zayd) will pay the ransom of the child, and the value on the day of litigation will be considered, and the child is free, because he is walad al-maghrur (child of the deceived), who, by consensus of the Companions, is freed by his value. 'Maghrur' refers to a person who has intercourse with a woman relying on ownership or marriage, and a child is born, then the woman turns out to belong to another. ... And according to the three imams, he also recovers the 'aqr.)
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the case of a man who buys a slave-girl, she bears a child, and he claims the child as his own, but later the slave-girl is proven to belong to someone else. The child is free (by consensus of the Companions), and the father must pay the child's value as ransom. The value is assessed on the day of litigation because that is when the father's detention of the child becomes apparent. If the child dies before litigation, no ransom is due. If the father kills the child, he must pay its value. The father can recover from the seller the price of the slave-girl and the child's value (as part of the slave-girl), but not the 'aqr (dower-like compensation for using the slave-girl). However, the three imams (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar) hold that he can also recover the 'aqr.

Key Terms
مغرور (maghrur): A person who has intercourse with a woman relying on ownership or marriage, then the woman turns out to belong to someone else.
عقر (aqr): A compensation paid to the true owner of a slave-girl for the man's sexual enjoyment of her.
ولد المغرور (walad al-maghrur): The child born to a maghrur, which is free and ransomed by its father's payment of its value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The child is free; ransom is its value on the day of birth.
C) The child is free; ransom is its value on the day of litigation.
D) The child is free; no ransom is needed because the father is deceived.

Key Takeaway
The child of a maghrur is free by consensus of the Companions, and the father pays its value as ransom; the 'aqr (benefit compensation) is not recoverable in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Hanafi Ruling on Acknowledging '100 and a Dirham': Istihsan Overriding Qiyas
Inter-madhhab dispute on ambiguous acknowledgment with istihsan basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that saying 'I owe 100 and a dirham' obligates 101 dirhams, and identify the role of istihsan and custom ('urf) in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
When custom is overwhelming, istihsan overrides qiyas: '100 and a dirham' means 101 dirhams.

This passage tackles an ambiguous acknowledgment: a person says 'I owe 100 and a dirham.' Does this mean 101 dirhams, or 100 plus an unspecified item? The Hanafi school employs istihsan based on widespread custom to settle the ambiguity, differing from the Shafi'i school which adheres to strict qiyas. Let's explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contested Issue
The acknowledgment 'I owe 100 and a dirham' contains an ambiguous number '100' and a specific item 'dirham'. The dispute is whether the waw (and) requires that the 100 be interpreted separately from the dirham, or whether custom allows the dirham to explain the 100.
The same structure appears in other ambiguous acknowledgments like '100 and a cloth'.
2
Understand the Qiyas Ruling
By pure qiyas (analogy), the waw of conjunction implies a difference between the conjoined items. Thus, '100' remains ambiguous and must be clarified by the acknowledger, just as in the case of '100 and a cloth' where the 100 is not automatically taken as dirhams.
Imam al-Shafi'i and a narration from Imam Ahmad follow this qiyas.
3
Explain the Hanafi Istihsan Exception
The Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) because dirhams are overwhelmingly frequent in debts and prices. Custom (urf) treats the word 'dirham' as explanatory of the ambiguous number, so the acknowledgment is understood as 101 dirhams immediately.
This istihsan is based on the high frequency of transactions involving dirhams.
4
Compare the Opposing School's Argument
Imam al-Shafi'i (and one narration of Ahmad) argue that the waw linguistically demands difference, so '100' cannot be explained by the following 'dirham'. They require the acknowledger to clarify the meaning of 100.
The linguistic principle of waw al-'atf is central to their argument.
5
Note the Scope of the Istihsan
The istihsan only applies to items that are frequently used in obligations, such as dirhams, dinars, and grain. For rare items like cloth, the qiyas remains, and the acknowledger must clarify the ambiguous number.
The distinction is based on custom and frequency of use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله على مائة و درهم.. مقر نے اقرار کیا کہ میرے ذمہ اس کے سو اور درہم ہے۔ تو اس پر تمام درہم ہی لازم ہوں گے۔ یعنی ایک سو ایک۔ اور اگر اس نے یہ کہا کہ مجھ پر اس کا سو اور ایک کپڑا ہے۔ تو اس سے سو کی تفسیر کرائی جائے گی۔ کی سو سے کیا مراد ہے؟ درہم مراد نہیں یا کپڑے۔ یہی حکم له على ماته و ثوبان کا ہے۔ مقتضاء قیاس تو علی ماته و در هم میں بھی یہی ہے کہ ماتہ کی تفسیر کو مقر پر چھوڑا جائے۔ چنانچہ امام شافعی اور ایک روایت میں امام احمد اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ ایک سو تو مبہم ہے اور ایک درہم اس پر واو عاطفہ کے ساتھ معطوف ہے اس کی تغیر نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ عطف بیان کے لئے موضوع نہیں بلکہ وہ تو معطوف و معطوف علیہ کے درمیان مقتضی مغایرت ہے تو لفظ ما تہ اپنے ابہام پر باقی رہا۔ جیسے فصل ثانی یعنی له على ماته وثوب ہے۔ فلابد من المصير الى البيان.
قوله وجه الاستحسان وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ عادت لفظ در ہم ما تہ کابیان ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ لوگ لفظ درہم کو دوبارہ بانان قیل جانتے ہیں اور صرف ایک بارذ کر کرنے پر اکتفا کرتے ہیں اور یہ ان چیزوں میں ہوتا ہے جو کثیر الاستعمال ہوں اور کثرت استعمال کا حق اس وقت ہوتا ہے۔ جب کثرت اسباب کی وجہ سے وجوب فی الزمہ بکثرت ہو جیسے در اہم ودنانی، تکمیل موزون کہ یہ مسلم قرض اور شمن میں واجب فی الذمہ ہوتے ہیں۔ بخلاف شیاب اور غیر تکمیل وغیرہ موزون کے کہ ان کا وجب اتنی کثرت سے نہیں ہوتا اس لئے ثیاب اور غیر کیل اور غیر موزوں چیزوں میں ماہ کی تفسیر مقر پر موقوف ہوگی۔ اور درا ہم ودنانی وغیرہ میں موقوف نہ ہوگی۔
His statement: 'upon him 100 and a dirham'... The acknowledger acknowledged that upon him is 100 and a dirham. So upon him all dirhams are binding, i.e., 101. And if he said: upon me is 100 and a cloth, then he will be asked to explain what is meant by 100: does he mean dirhams or cloth? The same ruling applies to 'upon him 100 and two cloths'. The requirement of qiyas would be that in 'upon him 100 and a dirham' as well, the interpretation of 100 should be left to the acknowledger. Accordingly, Imam al-Shafi'i and in one narration Imam Ahmad hold this view. Because 100 is ambiguous and a dirham is conjoined with it by the conjunctive waw; it does not serve to explain, because the conjunctive is not intended for explanation but rather requires difference between the conjoined and the conjoined-to. So the word '100' remains ambiguous, like the second category, i.e., 'upon him 100 and a cloth'. So resort to explanation is necessary. His statement: the reason for istihsan. The reason for istihsan is that the custom is for the word 'dirham' to explain 100, because people know the word dirham by repetition and are content with mentioning it once. This occurs in things of frequent use, and the right of frequent use is when obligation in the dhimmah becomes frequent due to frequency of causes, like dirhams and dinars, which are complete weighed items that are obliged in the dhimmah for debts and prices. Contrary to cloths and incomplete weighed items, whose obligation does not occur so frequently. Therefore, in cloths and non-grain and non-weighed items, the interpretation of 100 is left to the acknowledger. In dirhams and dinars etc., it is not left to him.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage deals with ambiguous acknowledgments (iqrar) where the debtor says 'I owe 100 and a dirham'. The Hanafi position, based on istihsan, is that this means 101 dirhams in total. The qiyas (analogy) would suggest that '100' remains ambiguous and must be explained by the acknowledger, as in the case of '100 and a cloth'. However, because dirhams are used so frequently in debts and prices, the custom ('urf) is that the word 'dirham' after '100' actually explains the '100' to be dirhams. This is istihsan (juristic preference) overriding qiyas. The Hanafis differ from Imam al-Shafi'i and a narration from Imam Ahmad, who stick to the qiyas and require explanation. The passage also distinguishes between items that are commonly weighed/measured (like dirhams, dinars, grains) and those that are not (like cloth), showing that the istihsan applies only to the former.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that abandons qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or equity.
مقتضى قياس (muqtada qiyas): The ruling required by analogical reasoning before considering istihsan.
عطف ('atf): Grammatical conjunction using waw; implies that the conjoined items are separate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if someone says 'I owe you 100 and a dirham', how much does he owe?
A) He owes 100 and must explain what the 100 refers to.
B) He owes 101 dirhams.
C) He owes 100 dirhams plus one unspecified item.
D) He owes 1 dirham only.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, istihsan can override qiyas when strong custom clarifies an ambiguous acknowledgment, leading to a straightforward obligation of 101 dirhams.

Ruling on Acknowledging '100 and Three Garments'
Clarifies that saying '100 and three garments' means 103 garments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a debtor says 'I owe 100 and three garments' and explain the linguistic reason why the word 'garments' qualifies both numbers.

Core Idea
Without a conjunction, the noun after the final number explains all preceding numbers.

Imagine a debtor says 'I owe you 100 and three garments.' Does he owe 103 garments or 100 dirhams plus three garments? The Hanafi school, relying on a linguistic principle, rules that the word 'garments' after 'three' without a conjunction (waw) explains both ambiguous numbers. This lesson unpacks that ruling and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the debtor acknowledging? The ruling is that he owes 103 garments.
The act is the acknowledgement (iqrar).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is linguistic: the omission of the conjunction (harf al-‘atf) causes the final noun to explain both preceding numbers.
This is a proof from Arabic usage (lughah).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Arabic, when two ambiguous numbers are followed by a noun without a conjunction, that noun resolves both. Here, 'three garments' (thalāthat athwāb) means 3 garments, but the phrase '100 and three' (mi’ah wa thalāth) would normally mean 100 plus 3. However, the repetition of 'garments' is omitted after 100, but the final 'garments' after 'three' covers both because of the lack of a conjunction separating them.
Wajh al-dalalah: how the linguistic feature proves the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that only the 'three' is qualified by 'garments', leaving the 100 ambiguous.
The disagreement is over the scope of the explanatory noun.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon because it conforms to established Arabic usage and avoids ambiguity.
Al-Marghinani in Ashraf al-Hidayah confirms this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قـولـه مـانة و ثلثة النواب... اور اگر میر نے کہا له علي مائة و ثلثة اثواب تو سب کپڑے ہی لازم ہوں گے ۔ یعنی ایک سوتین کپڑے۔ امام شافعی کے یہاں تین کپڑے لازم ہوں گے۔ اور مائتہ کی تفسیر کرائی جائے گی۔ جیسا کہ اوپر مذکور ہوا۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ یہاں ما تہ اور ثلاث وعدم مہم ہیں۔ دونوں کی تفسیر کو ضرورت ہے اور اس نے ثلاثہ کے بعد لفظ اثواب بلا حرف عطف ذکر کیا ہے۔ تو یہ دونوں کی تفسیر ہوگئی۔ فكان كلها ثیابا۔
His statement: '100 and three garments'... And if the acknowledger said 'upon him 100 and three garments', then all are garments, i.e., 103 garments. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, only three garments are binding and the 100 would require interpretation. We say that here '100' and 'three' are both ambiguous. Both require interpretation, and the speaker mentioned the word 'garments' after 'three' without a conjunctive letter. So that serves as an interpretation for both. Therefore all are garments.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage addresses when someone says 'I owe 100 and three garments'. The Hanafi position is that the word 'garments' (athwab) after 'three' explains both the '100' and the 'three', because the speaker omitted the conjunction (waw) and directly said 'three garments'. This is understood as an adjectival or explanatory construction. Thus, the total owed is 103 garments. Imam al-Shafi'i would hold that '100' remains ambiguous and only the three garments are certain, so the acknowledger would have to clarify what the 100 refers to. The Hanafi reasoning is that the absence of the conjunction makes the noun explain both numbers, a common linguistic feature in Arabic.

Key Terms
بلا حرف عطف (bila harf 'atf): Without a conjunctive particle (like waw); here indicates that the noun explains the preceding numbers directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'I owe you 100 and three garments' (without repeating the conjunction), how many garments does he owe according to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) 3 garments, and 100 remains ambiguous
B) 100 garments plus 3 additional items
C) 103 garments
D) Only the three garments are binding

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when ambiguous numbers are followed by a noun without a conjunction, that noun qualifies all preceding numbers, creating a single obligation.

Ruling on Acknowledging Items in Containers: The Zarf-Mazruf Principle
Clarifies what is included when acknowledging something in a container

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for iqrar involving containers, distinguishing movable from immovable containers and identifying the effect of the preposition 'min'.

Core Idea
Acknowledging a contained item includes its movable container but not an immovable one, unless 'min' shows extraction.

When someone acknowledges a debt or property described as being 'in' something, what exactly is owed? The Hanafi school developed a detailed rule based on the nature of the container. This passage from al-Hidayah, relying on Imam Muhammad's al-Asl, explains the principle through multiple examples and notes a key difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf versus Imam Muhammad regarding immovable containers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Recognize that we are dealing with iqrar (acknowledgment) of a tangible item described as being in a container. The hukm is that the acknowledger must deliver the item and possibly the container.
The ruling derives from the principle that seizing a contained item necessarily involves the container if it is movable.
2
Understand the general rule: movable container includes both
If the container is movable (e.g., basket, sack, handkerchief), acknowledging the contained item makes both the item and the container binding. The reasoning is that taking possession of the contained item without the container is impossible.
This is based on the concept of ghasp (usurpation) as explained in al-Asl.
3
Apply the rule to examples
Go through each example: dates in a basket (both owed), food in a ship (both), wheat in a sack (both), cloth in a handkerchief (both). Also ring (band and stone), sword (blade, hilt, strap), bridal chamber (poles and covering) – these are included because the name encompasses all parts.
Custom (urf) determines what the name covers, e.g., 'ring' includes the stone.
4
Distinguish the exception: 'min' changes the ruling
If the acknowledger says 'I seized dates from a basket', the preposition 'min' indicates extraction. Only the extracted item (dates) is owed, not the basket.
The word 'min' has legal significance; it removes the container from the acknowledgment.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on immovable containers
When the container is immovable (e.g., stable, house), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that only the contained item is owed because the container is not guaranteeable by seizure. Imam Muhammad analogizes to movable containers and holds both are owed. The mufta bihi is the view of the two shaykhs.
The dispute is based on whether the illa (reason) of 'taking both' applies to immovables.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِتَمْرٍ فِي قَوْصَرَةٍ لَزِمَهُ التَّمْرُ وَالْقَوْصَرَةُ وَفَسَّرَهُ فِي الْأَصْلِ بِقَوْلِهِ غَصِبْتُ تَمْرًا فِي قَوْصَرَةٍ وَوَجْهُهُ أَنَّ الْقَوْصَرَةَ وِعَاءٌ وَظَرْت لَهُ وَغَصْبُ الشَّيْءِ وَهُوَ مَظْرُوفٌ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ بِدُونِ الظَّرْفِ فَيَلْزَمَانِهِ وَكَذَا الطَّعَامُ فِي السَّفِينَةِ وَالْحِنْطَةُ فِي الْجُوَالِقِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ غَضِبْتُ تَمُرًا مِنْ قَوْصَرَةٍ لِأَنَّ كَلِمَةَ مِنْ للانتِزَاعٍ فَيَكُونُ إِقْرَارٌ بِغَضَبِ الْمُنْزُوعِ قَالَ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِدَابَةٍ فِي اصْطَبَلِ لَزِمَهُ الدَّابَةِ خَاصَةٌ لِأَنَّ الْأَصْطَبَلَ غَيْرُ مَضْمُونِ بِالْغَصْبِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَابِى يُوسُفَ وَعَلَى قِيَاسِ قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٌ يَضْمَنُهُمَا وَمِثْلَهُ الطَّعَامُ فِي الْبَيْتِ. قَالَ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ لِغَيْرِهِ بِخَاتَمِ لَزِمَهُ الْحَلَقَةُ وَالْقَصُّ لَانَّ إِسْمَ الْخَاتَمِ يَشْمَلُ الْكُلَّ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ لَهُ بِسَيْفٍ فَلَهُ النَّصْلُ وَالْحَفْنُ وَالْحَمَائِلُ لِاَنَّ الْإِسْمَ يَنْطَوِي عَلَى الْكُلَّ وَمَنْ اَقَرَّ بِحَجَلَةٍ فَلَهُ الْعِيْدَانُ وَالْكِسْوَةُ لِإِطْلَانِ الْإِسْمِ عَلَى الْكُلِّ عُرْفًا وَإِنْ قَالَ غَصِبْتُ ثَوْبًا فِى مِنْدِيلِ لَزِمَاهُ جَمِيعًا لِأَنَّهُ ظَرْفٌ لِاَنَّ التَّوْبَ يُلَقُ فِيهِ وَكَذَا لَوْ قَالَ عَلَيَّ ثَوْبٌ فِي ثَوْبِ لِأَنَّهُ ظَرْفٌ بِخِلَافِ قَوْلِهِ دِرْهُمْ فِي دِرْهَم حَيْثُ يَلْزَمُهُ وَاحِدٌ لِأَنَّهُ ضَرْبٌ لَا ظَرْقْ
ترجمہ جس نے اقرار کیا چھواروں کا ٹوکری میں تو لازم ہوں گے اس کو چھوار نے مع زنبیل مبسوط میں اس کی تفسیر یوں کی ہے کہ مقر نے کہا کہ میں نے چھوارے زنبیل میں غصب کئے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ زنبیل ان کے لئے ظرف ہے اور شئی کو غصب کرنا درانحالیکہ وہ ظرف میں ہے بدون ظرف کے متحقق نہیں ہو سکتا تو دونوں لازم ہوں گے۔ ایسے ہی اناج ہے کشتی میں اور گیہوں گون میں۔ بخلاف اس کے جب کہا۔ کہ میں نے خرمہ غصب کئے زنبیل میں ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ من نکالنے کے لئے ہے تو یہ نکالی ہوئی چیز کے غصب کا اقرار ہوگا۔ جس نے اقرار کیا گھوڑے کا طویلہ میں تو لازم ہو گا اس پر صرف گھوڑا۔ کیونکہ طویلہ مضمون بالخصب نہیں ہوتا۔ شیخین کے نزدیک اور امام محمد کے قول پر قیاس کرنے سے دونوں کا ضامن ہونا چاہئے۔ ایسے ہی ہے اناج گھر میں جس نے اقرار کیا دوسرے کے لئے انگوٹھی کا تو لازم ہو گا اس کا حلقہ اور نگینہ۔ کیونکہ لفظ خاتم سب کو شامل ہے۔ جس نے اقرار کیا چھپر کھٹ کا تو اس کے لئے لکڑیاں اور پردہ ہو گا۔ کیونکہ عرف میں یہ لفظ کل پر بولا جاتا ہے۔ اگر کہا کہ میں نے غصب کیا ہے کپڑا۔ رومال میں تو دونوں لازم ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ رومال ظرف ہے اس لئے کہ کپڑا اس میں لپیٹا جاتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی اگر کہا کہ مجھ پر تھان ہے کپڑے میں کیونکہ کپڑ ا ظرف ہے۔ بخلاف اس قول کے کہ درہم ہے درہم میں کہ ایک ہی درہم لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو ضرب کا حساب ہے نہ کہ ظرف۔ تشريح ... قوله ومن اقر بتمر ایک شخص نے اقرار کیا کہ مجھ پر فلاں کے لئے چھوارے ہیں زنبیل میں ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام محمد نے اصل یعنی مبسوط میں اس مسئلہ کی تغییر غضب سے کی ہے۔ یعنی مقر نے یہ کہا کہ میں نے چھوارے زنبیل - نصب کئے ہیں تو اس اقرار میں مقر کے ذمہ چھوارے مع زنبیل یعنی ظرف اور مظروف دونوں لازم ہوں گے۔ اور اگر یوں اقرار کیا کہ مجھ پر فلاں کا جانور ہے اصطبل میں تو صرف جانور لازم ہوگا۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک یہاں بھی دونوں لازم ہوں گے۔ اس سلسلہ میں قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ جو چیز ظرف ہونے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہو اور اس کو منتقل کرنا ممکن ہو تو ایسی چیز کے اقرار میں ظرف اور مظروف دونوں لازم ہوتے ہیں۔ جیسے کھجور کا اقرار ٹوکری میں غلہ کا اقرارگون میں، کپڑے کا اقرار رومال میں وغیرہ اور اگر منتقل کرنا ممکن نہ ہو جیسے اصطبل وغیرہ تو شیخین کے نزدیک صرف مظروف لازم ہوگا۔ جیسے جانور وغیرہ۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک دونوں لازم ہوں گے اور اگر وہ چیز ظرف ہونے کی صلاحیت نہ رکھتی ہو تو صرف پہلی چیز لازم ہوگی۔ جیسے یوں کہتے کہ مجھ پر ایک درہم ہے درہم میں تو صرف پہلا در ہم لازم ہوگا۔ قوله غصبت من قوصرة .. اور اگر میر نے یہ کہا کہ غصبت من قوصرة یعنی میں نے رنبیل میں سے خرمہ غصب کئے تو صرف چھوپرے لازم ہوں گے زنبیل لازم نہ ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ کلمہ من انتزاع کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے تو منزوع یعنی جو چیز نکالی ہے اس کے غصب کا اقرار ہو گا ۔
He said: Whoever acknowledges dates in a basket, the dates and the basket are both incumbent upon him. And he explained it in al-Asl by his saying: 'I seized dates in a basket.' Its reasoning is that the basket is a container and a vessel for it, and seizing something while it is contained cannot be realized without the container, so both are incumbent. Similarly, food in a ship and wheat in a sack. Unlike when he says 'I seized dates from a basket', because the word 'min' is for extraction, so it is an acknowledgment of seizing the extracted item. He said: Whoever acknowledges an animal in a stable, only the animal is incumbent upon him, because the stable is not guaranteeable by seizure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, while according to the analogy of Muhammad's statement, he guarantees both. Similarly, food in a house. He said: Whoever acknowledges for another a ring, the ring [i.e., the band] and the stone are incumbent because the name 'ring' includes both. Whoever acknowledges for him a sword, he gets the blade, the hilt, and the strap because the name encompasses all. Whoever acknowledges a bridal chamber, he gets the poles and the covering because the name commonly applies to all. If he says 'I seized a cloth in a handkerchief', both are incumbent because it is a container, as cloth is folded in it. Similarly if he says 'upon me a cloth in a cloth', because it is a container. Unlike his saying 'a dirham in a dirham', where only one is incumbent because it is a calculation, not a container. Translation: Whoever acknowledged dates in a basket, the dates and the basket are incumbent upon him. In al-Mabsut, this is interpreted as the acknowledger saying 'I seized dates in a basket'. The reason is that the basket is a container, and seizing the contained thing without the container cannot be realized, so both are incumbent. Similarly, grain in a ship and wheat in a sack. Unlike if he said 'I seized dates from a basket', because 'min' indicates removal, so it is an acknowledgment of seizing the removed item. Whoever acknowledged a horse in a stable, only the horse is incumbent upon him, because the stable is not guaranteed by seizure according to the two shaykhs, while by analogy of Muhammad's statement, he should be guarantor of both. Similarly, grain in a house. Whoever acknowledged for another a ring, the band and the stone are incumbent because the word 'ring' includes all. Whoever acknowledged a cot, he gets the sticks and the curtain because in custom the word is used for all. If he said 'I seized a cloth in a handkerchief', both are incumbent because the handkerchief is a container, as cloth is folded in it. Similarly if he said 'upon me a cloth in a cloth', because it is a container. Unlike saying 'a dirham in a dirham', where one dirham is incumbent because it is a calculation, not a container. Commentary... His statement: 'Whoever acknowledged dates'... A person acknowledged that upon him for someone are dates in a basket. The author of Hidayah says that Imam Muhammad interpreted this issue with seizure in al-Asl, meaning the acknowledger said 'I seized dates in a basket'. In this acknowledgment, both dates and the basket are incumbent. If he acknowledged 'upon me is an animal in a stable', then only the animal is incumbent. According to Imam Muhammad, both are incumbent. The general principle is that if the container is capable of being transferred, then both container and contained are incumbent in the acknowledgment, like dates in a basket, grain in a sack, cloth in a handkerchief. If transfer is not possible, like a stable, then according to the two shaykhs only the contained is incumbent. According to Imam Muhammad, both are incumbent. If the item is not fit to be a container, like 'a dirham in a dirham', only the first is incumbent. His statement: 'I seized from a basket'... If the acknowledger said 'I seized dates from a basket', then only the dates are incumbent because 'min' indicates removal, so it is an acknowledgment of seizing what was removed.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage discusses iqrar (acknowledgment) when the subject is described as being 'in' a container. The general Hanafi rule is that if the container is something that can be possessed and transferred, acknowledging the contained item includes the container. For example, acknowledging dates in a basket makes both the dates and the basket binding. The reasoning is that one cannot take possession of the dates without also taking the basket. This is likened to ghasp (usurpation) where the container is also taken. However, if the container is immovable or not subject to possession (like a stable or a house), only the contained item is binding according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad holds that both are binding, analogizing to the movable case. Other examples include a ring (both band and stone), a sword (blade, hilt, strap), a bridal chamber (poles and covering), and a cloth in a handkerchief (both cloth and handkerchief). An exception is 'dirham in a dirham', which is a calculation (like '5 within 5') not a container, so only one dirham is owed. The passage also distinguishes saying 'dates in a basket' (both owed) from 'dates from a basket' (only dates owed) because 'min' indicates removal, so only the removed item is acknowledged.

Key Terms
ظرف (zarf): A container that can hold and be transferred; in this context, it determines whether both items are included in an acknowledgment.
مظروف (mazruf): The contained item, e.g., dates or cloth.
من (min): The preposition 'from' indicating removal; changes the ruling from including the container to only the extracted item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone acknowledges 'I owe you food in a ship', what is owed according to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Only the food
B) Both the food and the ship
C) Only the ship
D) The acknowledgment is invalid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule for acknowledging property 'in' a container hinges on whether the container is movable; if so, both are owed, unless 'min' indicates extraction.

Ruling on Acknowledging 'A Cloth Among Ten Cloths'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on interpreting 'fi' in iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the interpretation of 'fi' in iqrar and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When acknowledging 'a cloth in ten cloths,' the mufta bihi is one cloth because 'fi' means 'among,' not 'inside.'

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines a subtle linguistic dispute in the context of iqrar (acknowledgment). When a person says 'I owe a cloth in ten cloths,' does that mean one cloth or eleven? The answer hinges on how we interpret the Arabic preposition 'fi'. Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa understand it as 'among,' while Muhammad sees potential for 'containment.' Their proofs and the relied-upon ruling are explored here.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed statement
The iqrar phrase is 'a cloth in ten cloths.' The dispute is about how many cloths the debtor acknowledges: one or eleven?
The preposition 'fi' (في) is the source of ambiguity.
2
Examine linguistic evidence for each interpretation
Abu Yusuf (and Abu Hanifa) argue that 'fi' here means 'among' (used in Quran 89:29 'fadkhuli fi 'ibadi'). Muhammad argues that 'fi' can also mean 'in' as a container, and custom shows valuable cloths wrapped in multiple layers.
The Quranic usage supports Abu Yusuf's default.
3
Trace the tarjih mechanism
Later Hanafi authorities like al-Marghinani and al-Zayla'i prefer the view of the two elders (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) as the default interpretation.
This is an example of tarjih based on linguistic principle and authority.
4
Determine mufta bihi and practical effect
The relied-upon ruling: only one cloth is owed. The debtor's liability is lighter than under Muhammad's view.
This ikhtilaf has financial consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ قَالَ قَوْبٌ فِى عَشَرَةِ الْوَابِ لَمْ يَلْزَمُهُ إِلَّا ثَوْبٌ وَاحِدٌ عِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفٌ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ لَزِمَهُ أَحَدَ عَشَرَ ثَوْبًا لانَّ النَّفِيسَ مِنَ القِيَابِ قَدْيُلَقُ فِى عَشَرَةِ الْوَابِ فَامْكَنَ حَمْلُه عَلَى الطَّرْفِ
ترجمہ اگر کہا کہ ایک کپڑا ہے دس کپڑوں میں تو لازم نہ ہوگا۔ مگر ایک کپڑا امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک امام محمد فر ماتے ہیں کہ گیارہ کپڑے لازم ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ کبھی عمدہ کپڑا اس کپڑوں میں لپیٹا جاتا ہے تو اس کو ظرف پر محمول کرناممکن ہے۔ تشريح قوله ثوب في عشرة . ایک شخص نے اقرار کیا کہ مجھ پر فلاں کا ایک کپڑا ہے دس کپڑوں میں تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک صرف ایک کپڑا لازم ہوگا۔ امام صاحب کا بھی یہی قول ہے (کافی) علامہ زیلعی نے تبیین الحقائق میں اس کو امام ابو حنیفہ کا پہلا قول مانا ہے۔ امام محمد صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ گیارہ کپڑے لازم ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ بعض عمدہ ترین اور بیش بہا کپڑے کئی کئی کپڑوں میں لیٹے جاتے ہیں تو لفظ فی کو ظرف پر محمول کرنا ممکن ہے امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل وَلَابِي يُوْسُفَ أَنَّ حَرْفَ فِي يُسْتَعْمَلُ فِي الْبَيْنِ وَالْوَسْطِ أَيْضًا قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى فَادْخُلِي فِي عِبَادِي أَيْ بَيْنَ
If he says 'a cloth in ten cloths', only one cloth is incumbent according to Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: eleven cloths are incumbent, because sometimes a valuable cloth is folded in ten cloths, so it is possible to interpret it as a container. Translation: If he said 'a cloth in ten cloths', nothing is incumbent except one cloth according to Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: eleven cloths are incumbent, because sometimes a fine cloth is wrapped in ten cloths, so it can be interpreted as a container. Commentary: His statement 'a cloth in ten cloths'. A person acknowledged that upon him is a cloth for someone in ten cloths. According to Abu Yusuf, only one cloth is incumbent. Imam [Abu Hanifa] also holds this view (according to al-Kafi). Allama Zayla'i in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq considered this the first opinion of Abu Hanifa. Imam Muhammad says that eleven cloths are incumbent, because some very fine valuable cloths are wrapped in several cloths, so the word 'fi' can be interpreted as a container. The proof of Abu Yusuf is that the letter 'fi' is also used for 'between' and 'among', as Allah says 'Enter among My servants' meaning between.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific iqrar case: someone acknowledges 'I owe a cloth in ten cloths'. The disagreement among Hanafi imams is based on the interpretation of the preposition 'fi' (in/among). Imam Abu Yusuf holds that only one cloth is owed because 'fi' here means 'among', so it is simply specifying one cloth among ten. This is also attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa as his first opinion. Imam Muhammad, however, argues that 'fi' can mean 'in' as a container, so the acknowledgment could be interpreted as a valuable cloth wrapped inside ten cloths, in which case all eleven cloths are owed. The choice depends on whether the phrase is seen as a description of location (among) or a container (in). Abu Yusuf supports his view with a Quranic verse where 'fi' means 'among'. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa, that only one cloth is owed, because the default is to interpret 'fi' as 'among' unless there is a clear intention of containment.

Key Terms
في (fi): The preposition 'in' or 'among'; its ambiguity leads to ikhtilaf.
ظرف (zarf): Container; used here by Muhammad to argue that 'fi' implies containment, not just location among.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if someone acknowledges 'I owe a cloth in ten cloths', how many cloths does he owe?
A) One cloth
B) Ten cloths
C) Eleven cloths
D) The acknowledgment is invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when 'fi' appears in an iqrar without clarifying context, it is interpreted as 'among' unless custom indicates otherwise, resulting in the debtor owing only the specified item, not the surrounding items.

Iqrar with Numerical Range: The Dispute on Including Limits
Explaining Hanafi positions on iqrar with a numerical range

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on iqrar with a numerical range and identify the mufta bihi with its justification.

Core Idea
When someone confesses 'from one to ten', the amount due differs by imam: 9 (Abu Hanifa), 10 (Sahibayn), or 8 (Zufar).

When a debtor says 'I owe from one dirham to ten dirhams,' the exact amount owed is not immediately clear. The Hanafi school has three distinct positions on whether the lower limit, upper limit, both, or neither are included in the confession. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view and identifies the relied-upon ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the confession and the disputed amount
The iqrar is 'from one dirham to ten dirhams' (or 'between one and ten'). The dispute is over how many dirhams are due: 8, 9, or 10. The iqrar itself is binding; only the amount is contested.
Confession is conclusive against the confessor; the range creates ambiguity.
2
Locate the three Hanafi positions and their reasoning
Abu Hanifa: 9 (includes lower limit only, because higher numbers depend on the lower). Sahibayn: 10 (both limits are existent and thus included). Zufar: 8 (neither limit is included, as limits are not part of the limited).
Sahibayn's view aligns with Shafi'i, Malik (one narration), and Ahmad (one view).
3
Analyze the basis of each view using istihsan and qiyas
Abu Hanifa uses istihsan for the first limit (inclusion) and qiyas for the second (exclusion). Sahibayn use istihsan for both limits. Zufar uses qiyas for both. Understanding how istihsan and qiyas operate here clarifies the differences.
Istihsan favours inclusion of the lower limit; qiyas favours exclusion.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its justification
The Sahibayn's view (10 dirhams) is the mufta bihi because it is from Zahir al-Riwayah, is more cautious (ihtiyat) in debt matters, and is adopted by later authorities like al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.
This resolution shows how later Hanafi scholarship settles intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

قوله من درهم الى عشرة .... ایک شخص نے اقرار کیا کہ مجھ پر ایک سے دس تک یا ما بین ایک سے دس تک ہے تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک نو لازم ہوں گے۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی ایک روایت میں امام مالک۔ ایک وجہ میں امام احمد کے نزدیک دس لازم ہوں گے ۔ گویا ابتداء وانتہا دونوں حدیں محدود میں داخل ہوں گی۔
وہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ دونوں حدوں کا موجود ہونا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ امر وجودی کے لئے معدوم شئی حد نہیں ہو سکتی۔ امام زفر کے نزدیک آٹھ لازم ہوں گے تو ان کے یہاں دونوں حدیں محدود میں داخل نہ ہوں گی۔ وہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بعض غائتیں مغیا میں داخل نہ ہوں گی۔ اور اگر مقر نے یہ کہا کہ فلاں کے لئے میرے گھر اس دیوار سے اس دیوار تک ہے تو بالا جماع مقرلہ کے لئے وہ حصہ ہوگا جو دونوں کے درمیان ہے۔ کیونکہ اصل یہی ہے کہ حدود محدود میں داخل نہیں ہوتیں۔ اس لئے کہ حد اور محدود کے درمیان مغائرت ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن پہلی صورت میں امام صاحب نے پہلی حدیعنی ابتداء کو اس لئے داخل مانا کہ مافوق الواحد یعنی دوسرے اور تیسرے کا وجود اول کے بغیر نہیں ہو سکتا۔ الحاصل غایت اولی میں امام صاحب کا قول استحسان ہے اور غایت ثانیہ میں قیاس اور صاحبین کا قول دونوں میں استحسان ہے اور امام زفر کا قول دونوں میں قیاس ہے۔
His saying: 'From one dirham to ten...' A person confessed that he owes from one to ten or between one and ten. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, nine are obligatory. According to the Sahibayn, and in one opinion Imam al-Shafi'i, in one narration Imam Malik, and in one view Imam Ahmad, ten are obligatory. So both the beginning and end limits are included in the limited. They say that both limits must exist because a non-existent thing cannot be a limit for an existent thing. According to Imam Zufar, eight are obligatory, so in his view neither limit is included in the limited. He says that some end-points are not included in the terminated. And if the confessor said: 'For so-and-so, my house from this wall to that wall', then by consensus the recipient gets what is between them, because the original principle is that limits are not included in the limited, due to the difference between limit and limited. But in the first case, Imam Abu Hanifa considered the first limit (the beginning) as included because numbers above one (i.e., two, three) cannot exist without the first. In summary, for the first limit, Imam's view is istihsan; for the second limit, it is qiyas. The Sahibayn's view is istihsan in both, and Imam Zufar's view is qiyas in both.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and inter-madhhab dispute concerning iqrar (confession) when the debtor says 'I owe from one dirham to ten dirhams.' The base matn likely stated the ruling briefly, and the commentator expands by presenting the positions of major imams. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that nine dirhams are due, excluding the upper limit (ten) but including the lower limit (one). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) along with Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik in one narration, and Imam Ahmad in one view rule that ten are due, including both limits. Imam Zufar rules that eight are due, excluding both limits. The commentator explains the reasoning: Abu Hanifa includes the lower limit because numbers above it depend on it (without one, two and three cannot exist), but excludes the upper limit because the limit itself is not part of the limited. The Sahibayn include both limits because both are existent and part of the range. Imam Zufar excludes both based on the general principle that boundaries are not included. The commentator notes that Abu Hanifa's view on the first limit is istihsan (juristic preference) and on the second is qiyas (analogy), while the Sahibayn's view is istihsan in both, and Zufar's is qiyas in both. The practical ruling (mufta bihi) is the Sahibayn's view, as it is the most cautious and commonly relied upon in fatwa.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission of a right or debt; a binding declaration that establishes liability.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable result.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, if a person says 'I owe from one dirham to ten dirhams', how many dirhams are due?
A) 8 dirhams
B) 9 dirhams
C) 10 dirhams
D) It depends on the intention of the confessor

Key Takeaway
For iqrar from one to ten, the mufta bihi is ten dirhams, following the Sahibayn's view based on istihsan and caution.

Iqrar for a Fetus with a Valid Cause
Explaining iqrar for a fetus when a valid cause is mentioned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of iqrar for a fetus when a valid cause is mentioned, and identify the conditions for its validity and binding effect.

Core Idea
An iqrar for a fetus is valid only if a possible cause of ownership is stated; it becomes binding upon live birth.

This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on iqrar (confession of debt) made in favor of a fetus. It establishes that such an iqrar is valid when accompanied by a valid cause (sabab salih) such as bequest or inheritance. The ruling also specifies the conditions for the iqrar to become binding and the consequences if the child is stillborn. Understanding this helps prevent confusion between valid and impossible causes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is iqrar (confession) made for a fetus. The ruling is sahih (valid) if a valid cause is mentioned.
2
Understand the role of the cause (sabab)
The cause must be salih li thubut al-milk, such as wasiyyah or irth. An impossible cause makes the iqrar void.
Example of impossible cause: the fetus sold property.
3
Note the conditions for binding
The fetus must have existed at the time of iqrar (known by gestation period) and must be born alive.
Minimum 6 months, maximum 2 years for a woman in iddah.
4
Analyze the consequences of stillbirth
If stillborn, the money goes back to the testator or deceased's estate, and the iqrar remains valid for them.
Imam Malik differs; see madhhab dispute.
5
Distinguish the case of an infant (radhi')
A radhi' can have transactions via a guardian, so iqrar with a cause like sale is valid, unlike a fetus.
The fetus has no guardian before birth.

Chapter: He said: Whoever says to the fetus of so-and-so woman: upon me is one thousand dirhams, then if he says: So-and-so bequeathed to him, or his father died and he inherited it, then the iqrar is valid because he confessed with a cause suitable for establishing ownership for him. Then if she gives birth to him alive within a period known that he existed at the time of iqrar, it becomes binding upon him. And if she gives birth to him dead, then the money belongs to the testator or the deceased until it is divided among his heirs, because in reality it is an iqrar for them, and it only transfers to the fetus after birth, and it did not transfer. And if she gives birth to two children alive, then the money is between them. And if the confessor says: He sold to me or he lent to me, nothing is binding upon him because he stated an impossible cause. Translation: Chapter: Whoever says that upon me is a thousand dirhams for the fetus of so-and-so. So if he says that so-and-so bequeathed to him or his father died and he is his heir, then the iqrar is valid because he confessed with a valid cause for proof of ownership for him. Then if she gives birth to a living child after such a period that it is known that at the time of iqrar he existed in the womb, then the iqrar becomes binding. And if she gives birth to a dead child, then the money belongs to the testator or the deceased, until it is divided among the heirs, because this iqrar is in reality for them; it only transfers to the fetus after birth, but it did not transfer. And if she gives birth to two living children, then the money is shared between them. And if the confessor says: The fetus sold to me or lent to me, then nothing is binding upon him because he stated a cause that is impossible. ... (Continued commentary in Urdu).
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding iqrar (confession) for a fetus (haml). The matn states the ruling and the commentary expands it with conditions and examples. The ruling: If someone confesses that he owes 1000 dirhams to the fetus of a specific woman, and he explains a valid cause such as a bequest or inheritance, the iqrar is valid. The fetus must be born alive within a period that confirms its existence at the time of iqrar (minimum 6 months, maximum 2 years for a woman in iddah). If born dead, the money goes back to the testator or deceased's estate. If twins, the money is shared equally. If the confessor mentions an impossible cause (e.g., the fetus sold him something or lent him money), the iqrar is void because a fetus cannot transact. The commentary addresses a question: why is this not considered retraction of iqrar? The answer: It is not retraction but an explanation of the cause, because some ignorant people mistakenly think a fetus has legal capacity. Another question: if a suckling infant (radhi') cannot transact either, why is iqrar for him valid? The answer: A suckling infant can be represented by a guardian (wali or qadi), so transactions via a deputy are possible, whereas a fetus cannot have a deputy before birth.

Key Terms
حمل (haml): Fetus or unborn child in the womb; considered a potential legal entity with limited capacity.
رضیع (radhi'): Suckling infant; a child who is nursing and lacks full legal capacity, but can have a guardian.
سبب صالح (sabab salih): A valid cause that can establish ownership, such as bequest (wasiyyah) or inheritance (irth).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Someone says: 'I owe 1000 dirhams to the fetus of Fatimah because her father bequeathed it.' If the child is stillborn, what happens to the money according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The iqrar is void and nothing is owed.
B) The money goes to Fatimah's father's heirs.
C) The money goes to Fatimah.
D) The iqrar is valid but payment is postponed until next pregnancy.

Key Takeaway
An iqrar for a fetus is valid if a possible cause of ownership is stated; it becomes binding upon live birth within the gestation period, but if stillborn, the money reverts to the cause's source.

Ambiguous Iqrar: Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad
Dispute on validity of ambiguous iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on ambiguous iqrar and apply the mufta bihi view in a given scenario.

Core Idea
An ambiguous confession is valid because it is a proof; the Hanafi school follows Muhammad's view.

When someone says 'I owe something' without specifying the amount or cause, is that a valid confession? Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani disagreed. This lesson breaks down their reasoning and shows which view prevails in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the dispute is about ambiguous iqrar (mubham iqrar) – a confession lacking clarity in amount, cause, or recipient.
2
State each imam's position
Abu Yusuf: invalid (la yasihh). Muhammad: valid (yasihh). Note that both are Hanafi imams.
3
Analyze the dalil for Muhammad
Muhammad argues that iqrar is a hujjah (proof) and must be given effect (yu'mal). Ambiguity does not nullify it; the minimum possible amount can be enforced.
This is a talil (reason-based) argument.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf holds that ambiguity leads to uncertainty and disputes, so the iqrar is invalid to avoid conflict.
He prioritizes clarity over literal enforcement.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: if someone says 'I owe something', Abu Yusuf says nothing is owed; Muhammad says a minimum debt is owed. The mufta bihi is Muhammad's view because it upholds the binding nature of a confession.
This is the relied-upon position in fatwa.

Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning ambiguous iqrar (mubham iqrar), where the confessor does not specify the cause or details of the debt. Abu Yusuf rules that ambiguous iqrar is invalid (la yasihh) because ambiguity prevents clarity of the right. Muhammad al-Shaybani rules that it is valid (yasihh) because iqrar is a hujjah (legal proof) and must be given effect (yu'mal) as much as possible. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school is the view of Muhammad, as it is more in line with the principle of enforcing contracts and confessions. The commentator does not elaborate further in this excerpt, but the ikhtilaf is clear: Abu Yusuf requires clarity to avoid disputes, while Muhammad prioritizes the binding nature of the confession itself.

Key Terms
مبہم اقرار (mubham iqrar): Ambiguous confession where the confessor does not specify the amount, cause, or recipient clearly.
حجت (hujjah): Proof or evidence; in legal context, a binding argument that establishes a right.

Ruling on Ambiguous Iqrar and the Dispute Between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf
Dispute on whether ambiguous iqrar without specifying cause is valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on ambiguous iqrar, identify the proofs of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf, and state the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
An ambiguous iqrar is valid when interpreted on a valid cause; Imam Muhammad's view prevails over Abu Yusuf's restriction to trade.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of an ambiguous iqrar (acknowledgment) where the person confessing does not specify the cause (sabab) of the liability. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that such an iqrar is valid and must be interpreted on a valid cause, while Imam Abu Yusuf argues that it is only valid if linked to trade. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to handle ambiguous legal declarations and appreciate the role of qiyas within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the ruling of Imam Muhammad (valid) and Imam Abu Yusuf (invalid unless linked to trade) regarding an ambiguous iqrar.
Also note that Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to agree with Abu Yusuf, and Imam Malik and Ahmad agree with Muhammad.
2
Identify the evidence for each
Imam Muhammad argues that iqrar is a shar'i proof that must be given effect; it can be interpreted on a valid cause like bequest or inheritance. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that an absolute iqrar is presumed to be for trade, based on qiyas to the iqrar of a slave permitted to trade or a mutual partner.
Abu Yusuf's analogy is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's qiyas
Examine his analogy: the asl is the case of a slave permitted to trade or a partner, where the iqrar is always interpreted as for trade. The far' is the ambiguous iqrar of an ordinary person. The illa is that the iqrar is absolute and the default cause is trade. Determine whether the illa applies universally.
Imam Muhammad objects that trade is not the only possible cause; other valid causes exist.
4
Evaluate Muhammad's response
Muhammad counters that the analogy is weak because trade is not the predominant cause; iqrar can arise from many valid causes like bequest, inheritance, or loan. His principle is to preserve the effect of the iqrar by interpreting it broadly on a valid cause (sabab salih).
This reflects the Hanafi preference for giving effect to declarations when possible.
5
Determine the thamarah and tarjih
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that under Muhammad's view an ambiguous iqrar is always valid and binding; under Abu Yusuf's view it is invalid unless the context indicates trade. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Muhammad's view, as it aligns with the principle of giving effect to iqrar and is adopted by the majority of later Hanafis.
This tarjih is supported by the fact that Imams Malik, Ahmad, and the stronger Shafi'i view also agree with Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدْ أَمْكَنَ بِالْحَمْلِ عَلَى السَّبَبِ الصَّالِحِ وَلَا بِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّ الْإِقْرَارَ مُطْلَقَه يَنْصَرِفُ إِلَى الْإِقْرَارِ . التِّجَارَةِ وَلِهَذَا حُمِلَ اِقْرَارُ الْعَبْدِ الْمَادُونِ وَاحِدِ الْمُتَفَاوَضَيْنِ عَلَيْهِ فَيَصِيرُ كَمَا إِذَا صَرَّحَ بِهِ. ترجمہ اور گرا را کو ہم کھا توصیح ہو گا اما اوایس کے نزدیک امام نے فرمایاکہ یہ ہوگا کیونکہ قر ار وی توں میں سے ہے تو اسکو عمل دلا نا ضروری ہے اور وہ ممکن ہے سبب صالح پر محمول کرنے سے امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مطلق اقرار اسی کی طرف منصرف ہوتا ہے جو تجارت کے سبب سے ہو اسی لئے عبد مازون اور مفاوضین میں سے ایک شریک کا اقرار اسی پر محمول ہوتا ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا۔ جیسے گویا اس نے تصریح کردی۔ تشریح قولہ خان اہم ۔ اگر مقر نے اقرار کو ہم رکھا یعنی صالح یا غیر صالح کوئی سبب بیان نہیں کیا تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اقرار صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ بقول بعض امام ابوحنیفہ بھی اس کے قائل ہیں۔ اور امام شافعی کا بھی یہی قول ہے۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک اقرار بہر صورت صحیح ہے۔ امام مالک واحمد بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اور امام شافعی کا بھی اصح قول یہی ہے۔ کیونکہ اقرار بھی شرعی حجتوں میں سے ایک حجت ہے تو جہاں تک ممکن ہو عمل دلانا ضروری ہے۔ پس مہم ہونے کی صورت میں کسی سبب صالح (وصیت یا میراث پر محمول کر لیا جائے گا۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مطلق اقرار ایسے ہی اقرار کی جانب منصرف ہوتا ہے جو بسبب تجارت ہو۔ چنانچہ عبد مازون یا متفاوفین میں سے کوئی ایک شریک اگر کوئی مطلق اقرار کرے۔ تو سبب تجارت پر محمول کیا جاتا ہے۔ پس مقر کا مہم اقرار ایسا ہو گیا کہ گویا اس نے تصریح کردی کہ حمل کا یہ مال مجھ پر تجارت کی وجہ سے لازم ہے اور چونکہ اس طرح کا صریح اقرار باطل ہے۔ تو مبہم اقرار بھی باطل ہوگا۔
And it is possible by carrying it upon a valid cause. And according to Abu Yusuf, an absolute iqrar is diverted to iqrar of trade. Therefore, the iqrar of a slave who is permitted to trade (ma'dhun) and one of the partners in a mutual partnership (mutafawidhan) is carried upon it, so it becomes as if he explicitly stated it. Translation: And for an ambiguous iqrar, it will be clarified. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the Imam said that this will be [valid] because iqrar is among the [legal] proofs, so it is necessary to give it effect. And that is possible by carrying it upon a valid cause. Imam Abu Yusuf's evidence is that an absolute iqrar is diverted to that which is due to trade. For this reason, the iqrar of a permissible slave (abd ma'dhun) and one of the two mutual partners is carried upon it. So this becomes as if he explicitly stated it. Commentary: If the person making iqrar left it ambiguous, meaning he did not mention any cause, valid or invalid, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf the iqrar will not be valid. According to some, Imam Abu Hanifa also held this view, and Imam Shafi'i also held this. According to Imam Muhammad, the iqrar is valid in any case. Imam Malik and Ahmad also held this, and the more correct view of Imam Shafi'i is also this. Because iqrar is one of the shar'i proofs, so it is necessary to give it effect as much as possible. So in the case of ambiguity, it will be carried upon a valid cause (like bequest or inheritance). Imam Abu Yusuf's evidence is that an absolute iqrar is diverted to iqrar due to trade. Thus, if a permissible slave or one of the mutual partners makes an absolute iqrar, it is carried upon a trade cause. So the ambiguous iqrar becomes as if he explicitly stated that this property is due to trade. And since such an explicit iqrar is invalid, the ambiguous iqrar is also invalid.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of an ambiguous iqrar (acknowledgment) where the person confessing does not specify the cause (sabab) of the liability. The text begins by stating that according to Imam Abu Yusuf, an absolute iqrar is presumed to be related to trade (tijarah). He analogizes this to the case of a slave permitted to trade (abd ma'dhun) or a partner in a mutual partnership (mutafawidh), whose absolute iqrar is always interpreted as arising from trade. Therefore, if a person makes an ambiguous iqrar, it is treated as if he explicitly stated that the liability is due to trade, which is a valid basis. However, Imam Muhammad argues that any ambiguous iqrar is valid regardless, because iqrar is a shar'i proof and must be given effect wherever possible; it should be interpreted on a valid cause such as bequest or inheritance. The commentary adds that Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to agree with Abu Yusuf, while Imam Malik, Ahmad, and the stronger view of Shafi'i agree with Muhammad. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that under Abu Yusuf's view, the iqrar is invalid if no valid cause is plausible; under Muhammad's view, it is always valid. The relied‑upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but later Hanafi practice tends toward Muhammad's view for flexibility.

Key Terms
اقرار مطلق (iqrar mutlaq): An acknowledgment (iqrar) made without specifying the cause or basis of the liability.
سبب صالح (sabab salih): A valid cause for liability, such as a debt from sale, loan, bequest, or inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is suspended until the cause is clarified.

Key Takeaway
Imam Muhammad's view that an ambiguous iqrar is valid and interpreted on a valid cause is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Iqrar Regarding a Fetus of a Slave-Girl or Sheep
Ruling on iqrar of a fetus with justification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on iqrar of a fetus and explain why it is valid even without an explicit cause.

Core Idea
An iqrar of a fetus is valid as long as a plausible legal basis exists, such as a bequest.

This lesson addresses a specific case in Hanafi mu'amalat: when someone acknowledges (iqrar) that a fetus of a slave-girl or a sheep belongs to another person. At first glance, such an acknowledgment might seem invalid because the fetus is not yet a separately existing entity. However, the Hanafi school upholds its validity by interpreting it as a potential bequest from a third party. This illustrates a broader principle: iqrar is given effect wherever a plausible legal interpretation is possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is iqrar (acknowledgment) of a fetus for another person. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) and binding (lazim).
2
Recognize the apparent problem
The fetus is not yet a separate legal entity; one might question how ownership can be claimed or acknowledged.
This is the common misunderstanding the lesson addresses.
3
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
The iqrar can be interpreted as an acknowledgment of a bequest from a deceased person. This gives it a valid legal basis (wajh sahih).
The phrase 'wa lahu wajh sahih' indicates a valid perspective.
4
Note the consensus
The commentary states that this ruling is by consensus (bil-ittifaq) among the Hanafi imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
No intra-Hanafi dispute exists.
5
Apply the principle
This case shows that iqrar is upheld whenever it can be interpreted in a legally plausible manner, even without specifying the cause. This aligns with the Hanafi preference for giving effect to declarations.
Compare with iqrar of a human fetus for lineage, which follows different rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِحَمْلِ جَارِيَةٍ أَوْ حَمْلٍ شَاةٍ لِرَجُلٍ صَحَ إِقْرَارُهُ وَلَزِمَهُ لِاَنَّ لَهُ وَجْهًا صَحِيحًا وَهُوَ الْوَصِيَّةُ بِهِ مِنْ جِهَةِ غَيْرِهِ فَحُمِلَ عَلَيْهِ. ترجمہ اور اگر اقرار کیا باندی یا بکری کے حمل کا کسی کے لئے تو اقرار صحیح ہے اور اس پر لازم ہے۔ کیونکہ اس اقرار کی وجہ مسیح موجود ہے اور وہ غیر کی طرف سے اس حمل کی وصیت ہے تو اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح: اگر کوئی شخص کسی کے لئے حمل کا اقرار کر لے تو اقرار بالاتفاق صحیح ہے خواہ وہ باندی کا حمل ہو یا کسی جانور کا) اگر چہ مقر اس کا کوئی سبب بیان نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ اس اقرار کی وجہ صحیح ممکن ہے۔ بایں طور ہو سکتا ہے کسی مرنے والے نے اس کی وصیت کی ہو اور اس ے ورثہ کو اقرار ہو کہ یہ عمل فلاں کے لئے ہے۔ لہذا اس کو جواز پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔
He said: Whoever acknowledges the fetus of a slave-girl or the fetus of a sheep for a man, his acknowledgment is valid and binding upon him, because it has a valid aspect, which is the bequest of it from another direction, so it is carried upon that. Translation: And if he acknowledges the fetus of a slave-girl or a sheep for someone, then the acknowledgment is valid and binding upon him, because this acknowledgment has a valid cause exists, and that is the bequest of this fetus from another person, so it will be carried upon it. Commentary: If a person acknowledges a fetus for someone, the acknowledgment is valid by consensus, whether it is the fetus of a slave-girl or an animal, even if the person does not mention any cause. Because a valid cause for this acknowledgment is possible. It can be that a deceased person bequeathed it, and the heirs acknowledge that this fetus is for so-and-so. Therefore, it will be carried upon permissibility.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a straightforward ruling statement. The author (Imam al-Quduri or the matn) states that if a person makes an iqrar (acknowledgment) regarding a fetus (haml) of a slave-girl or a sheep, the iqrar is valid and binding. The reason given is that there is a valid way to interpret it: the fetus could have been bequeathed to that person by someone else, and the person making the iqrar is merely acknowledging that fact. The commentary adds that this ruling is by consensus (bil-ittifaq) among the Hanafi imams. Even if the person does not specify the cause, the iqrar is upheld because a plausible valid cause exists. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of giving effect to iqrar wherever possible (haml 'ala al-sabab al-salih).

Key Terms
حمل (haml): Fetus; an unborn offspring of a human or animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
An iqrar of a fetus of a slave-girl or animal is valid in Hanafi law if it can be interpreted plausibly as a bequest, even without explicit cause.

Iqrar with a Condition of Option (Khiyar) – Condition Void but Iqrar Binding
Ruling on iqrar with a condition of option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a condition of option (khiyar) in an iqrar is void and why the iqrar itself remains binding under Hanafi law.

Core Idea
An iqrar is an information, not a contract; it cannot be conditioned on an option to rescind.

When someone acknowledges a debt or liability, they may try to attach a condition giving themselves an option to cancel the acknowledgment within a few days. This may seem reasonable, but Hanafi fiqh treats it quite differently. The distinction lies in the nature of iqrar: it is an informational statement (ikhbar), which is either true or false, not a contract that can be rescinded. In this lesson, you will learn the precise legal reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
The passage discusses a person who makes an iqrar (acknowledgment) and attaches a condition of khiyar (option to rescind). The ruling: the condition is void (batil), but the iqrar itself is valid and binding (lazim).
This applies to various types of iqrar: debt, usurpation, sale, loan.
2
Understand the nature of iqrar as ikhbar
Iqrar is classified as an informational statement (ikhbar). It reports a pre-existing fact. If true, it is binding; if false, it must be rejected. Its truth value is independent of any choice.
The binding force of iqrar comes from the formula used (e.g., 'alayya).
3
Understand the nature of khiyar
Khiyar is a right to rescind a contract (faskh al-aqd). It is designed for contracts (uqud) where the parties can decide to cancel or confirm the deal. It changes the contractual status.
In contracts, khiyar affects enforceability; in iqrar, there is no contract to rescind.
4
Apply the qiyas: why khiyar cannot apply to iqrar
The passage argues by analogy (qiyas): since iqrar is an information, and information is either true or false, allowing an option would imply that its truth can be suspended—this is illogical. Thus, khiyar is incompatible.
The condition is void because it contradicts the nature of ikhbar.
5
Note the practical outcome
The void condition does not affect the iqrar. The liability remains binding because the binding formula (sighah mulzimah) is sufficient, and the void condition cannot annul it.
This ensures iqrar remains a reliable evidence in legal proceedings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِشَرْطِ الْخَيَارِ بَطَلَ الشَّرْطُ لِاَنَّ الْخَيَارَ لِلْفَسْخِ وَالْإِخْبَارُ لَا يَحْتَمِلُهُ وَلَزِمَهُ الْمَالُ لِوُجُودِ الصَّيْعَةِ الْمُلْزِمَةِ وَلَمْ يَنْعَدِمُ بِهَذَا الشَّرْطِ الْبَاطِلِ. ترجمہ: جس نے شرط خیار کا اقرار کیا تو شرط باطل ہے۔ کیونکہ خیار برائے فسخ ہوتا ہے۔ اور اخبار اس کا متحمل نہیں ہے اور مال کا لازم ہونا صیغہ ملزمہ کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور شرط باطل کی وجہ سے لزوم نہیں ٹوٹے گا۔ تشریح: قوله بشرط الخيار اگر زید نے بکر کے لئے قرض یا غصب یاور بیعت یا عاریت ( قائمہ یا مستہلکہ ) کا اقر ار اس شرط پر کیا کہ مجھے تین روز تک اپنے اقرار میں اختیار ہے تو اقرار حیح ہوگا اور شرط باطل ہوگی۔ بطلان شرط تو اس لئے ہے کہ خیار اس غرض سے ہوتا ہے کہ جب چاہے مسخ کر دے اور اقرار اخبار ہے جو قابل خیار نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ خبر اگر صادق ہے۔ تو وہ واجب العمل ہے خواہ وہ اختیار کرے یا نہ کرے۔ اور اگر کا ذب ہے تو وہ واجب الرد ہے جو اس کے اختیار وعدم اختیار سے متغیر نہیں ہوسکتی۔ شرط خیار کا اثر و عقود میں ہوتا ہے کہ اس سے عقد کی صفت متغیر ہو جاتی ہے اور صاحب خیار کو فسخ عقد اور امضاء عقد کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ رہا اقرار کا صیح ہوکر مال کالا زم ہونا سو اس لئے کہ جس لفظ سے اس نے اقرار کیا ہے یعنی علی وغیرہ و وصیغہ ملزمہ ہے اور لزوم باطل شرط سے معدوم نہیں ہو سکتا۔
He said: Whoever makes an acknowledgment (iqrar) with a condition of option (khiyar), the condition is void because khiyar is for rescission, and information (ikhbar) does not admit it. And the liability is binding upon him due to the existence of the binding formula, and it is not annulled by this void condition. Translation: Whoever made an acknowledgment with a condition of option, the condition is void because khiyar is for rescission, and an information (akhbar) cannot accommodate it. And the property becomes binding due to the binding formula, and it is not annulled by this void condition. Commentary: If Zayd makes an iqrar for Bakr regarding a debt, usurpation, sale, or loan (either existing or consumed) with the condition that he has an option for three days, then the iqrar is valid and the condition is void. The invalidity of the condition is because khiyar is intended for rescission, and iqrar is an information (ikhbar) which cannot accommodate rescission. This is because if the information is true, it is binding whether he exercises the option or not; if it is false, it must be rejected, which does not change with his option. The effect of khiyar in contracts is that the nature of the contract changes, giving the person with the option the right to rescind or confirm. As for the iqrar being valid and the property binding, it is because the words he used (like 'alayya, etc.) are a binding formula, and bindingness cannot be annulled by a void condition.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a person makes an iqrar (acknowledgment) but attaches a condition of khiyar (option), e.g., 'I owe you this amount, but I have the option to cancel my acknowledgment within three days.' The ruling is that the condition is void (batil) because khiyar is designed for rescinding a contract, but iqrar is an information (ikhbar) about a pre-existing liability. An information is either true or false; if true, it is binding regardless of any option, and if false, it must be rejected. Therefore, the option has no effect. However, the iqrar itself remains valid and binding because the formula used (e.g., 'li 'alayya') is a binding expression. The void condition does not affect the binding nature of the iqrar. The commentary clarifies that this applies to various types of iqrar: for debt, usurpation, sale, or loan. The key distinction is between contracts (uqud), which can accommodate khiyar, and informational statements (ikhbar), which cannot.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): Option or right to rescind a contract within a specified period.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession of a right or liability against oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person makes an iqrar (acknowledgment) with a condition that he has an option to cancel it within three days?
A) The iqrar is valid and the condition is also valid.
B) The iqrar is void due to the invalid condition.
C) The condition is void, but the iqrar remains binding.
D) The iqrar is suspended until the option period expires.

Key Takeaway
A condition of khiyar in an iqrar is void because iqrar is an informational statement, not a contract; the iqrar remains binding.

The Law of Istithna (Exception) in Iqrar
Ruling and proof on istithna in iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a connected exception in iqrar, distinguish valid and invalid exceptions, and explain the Hanafi position on exception of the majority with its proof.

Core Idea
A connected exception in iqrar leaves only the remainder binding; excepting the whole is a retraction, but excepting most is valid by Quranic proof.

This passage establishes the core rules of making an exception (istithna) when acknowledging a debt. The author lays down that as long as the exception is immediately connected to the acknowledgment, it is valid and only the stated remainder is owed. A key dispute arises over whether one can except the majority (e.g., nine hundred out of a thousand). The Hanafi school, relying on Quranic verses, affirms its validity — a position that has practical consequences for financial acknowledgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what legal act is being discussed (making an exception in an iqrar) and the basic ruling (it is valid if connected, and only the remainder is binding).
The exception must be part of the same sentence or immediately connected.
2
Locate the conditions for validity
Identify the condition that the exception must be connected (muttasil). A gap invalidates it unless due to necessity like coughing.
Disconnected exception makes the full iqrar binding.
3
Examine the boundary case: excepting the whole
If the exception covers the entire amount, it leaves no remainder and is considered a retraction (ruju'), so the full iqrar stands.
This is analogous to the rule in divorce.
4
Analyze the dispute on majority exception
Some scholars (Zufar, Ahmad, a narration from Abu Yusuf) hold that excepting the majority is invalid because Arabs do not use it. The Hanafi majority validates it.
The dispute is based on linguistic custom versus Quranic evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi position relies on Quranic verses where Allah excepts a majority (73:2-4, 15:39-40). This shows majority exception is linguistically valid and thus legally permissible.
The Quranic usage is considered the highest form of eloquence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كما في قوله لفلان على الف الاستمائة اب جو کچھ باقی رہے گا۔ وہ مقر پر لازم ہوگا۔لیکن کل کا استثناء کرنا میچ نہیں فاسد ہے (جو ہرہ) کیونکہ استثناء کے بعد کچھ نہ کچھ باقی رہناضروری ہے۔ فرا نحوی کے نزدیک اکثر کا استثنا بھی صحیح نہیں۔ کیونکہ اہل عرب اس کا تکلم نہیں کرتے ۔ امام زفر ، امام احمد اور ابن درستو به نحوی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اور غیر روایت اصول میں امام ابو یوسف سے بھی یہی مروی ہے۔ لیکن اکثر علماء کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اور دلیل جواز یہ آیت ہے قسـم الـلـيـل الا قليلا نصفه او انقص منه قليلا او زد عَلَيْهِ ( کھڑارہ رات کو مگر تھوڑا سا حصہ آدھی رات یا اس میں سے کم کر دے۔ تھوڑ اسا یا زیادہ کر اس پر ) اور اس سے زیادہ قوی دلیل وہ آیت ہے جو ابن حاجب نے مختصر الا الاصول میں ذکر کی ہے۔ یعنی " لاغوينهم اجمعين الا عبادك منهم المخلصین " ( راہ سے کھو دوں گا ان سب کو مگر جو تیرے چنے ہوئے بندے ہیں ) اس کے بعد فرمایا ' ان عبادى ليس لك عليهم من سلطن الا من اتبعك من الغاوين (جو میرے بندے ہیں تیرا ان پر کچھ زور نہیں مگر جو تیری راہ چلا بہکے ہوؤں میں )۔ وجه استدلال یہ ہے کہ مخلصین کی قلت ہے اور خاوین کی کثرت بدلیل قول باری "وما اكثر الناس ولو حرصت بمومنين" پھر یہ کہنا بھی غلط ہے کہ عرب نے اس کا تکلم نہیں کیا۔ بل تكلمت به العرب فقال الشاعر
Chapter on Exception (istithna) and what is in its meaning. He said: Whoever makes an exception (istithna) connected to his acknowledgment, the exception is valid and the remainder is binding upon him, because the exception together with the sentence is an expression of the remainder. But connection is necessary, whether he excepts a little or a lot. If he excepts the whole, the acknowledgment is binding upon him and the exception is void, because one speaks of what remains after the excepted thing, and there is no remainder after the whole, so it becomes a retraction (ruju'). The reasoning has passed in the chapter on divorce. Translation: Whoever makes an exception along with his iqrar, the exception is valid and the remainder is binding. Because the exception with the sentence indicates the remainder. But connectivity is necessary, whether the exception is small or large. If he excepts the whole, then the iqrar is binding and the exception is void, because exception is speaking of what remains after the excepted item, and after excepting the whole there is nothing left. So it becomes a retraction. The reasoning has passed in the book of divorce. Commentary: The chapter discusses modifiers of the effect of iqrar. The definition of istithna: it is derived from 'thana' meaning to exclude. It is speaking of the remainder after excluding some items from a number. The condition for validity is that the excepted item (mustathna) must be mentioned immediately after the general term (mustathna minhu). If there is a gap (except for necessity like coughing), it is invalid except according to Ibn Abbas. The ruling: if a person makes an exception of part of what he acknowledged, it is valid provided it is immediate, whether the exception is small (e.g., 'I owe a thousand except four hundred') or large (e.g., 'I owe a thousand except nine hundred'). The remainder is binding. If he excepts the whole, it is void because nothing remains. Some grammarians (e.g., al-Farra') and Imams Zufar, Ahmad, and Ibn Durustawayh consider exception of the majority invalid, because the Arabs did not use it. But the majority of scholars allow it, with evidence from Quranic verses: 'Stand the night except a little, half of it or reduce from it a little or add to it' (Quran 73:2-4) and 'I will surely mislead them all, except Your chosen servants among them' (Quran 15:39-40). The reasoning: 'mukhlisin' (sincere) are few and 'ghawin' (misguided) are many. Also it is incorrect to say that Arabs did not use it; a poet used it.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on istithna (exception) in the context of iqrar. It states the basic ruling: if a person makes an iqrar and immediately adds an exception (e.g., 'I owe you a thousand dirhams except one hundred'), the exception is valid and only the remainder (e.g., nine hundred) is binding. The exception must be connected (muttasil) to the iqrar without a significant gap. The ruling applies whether the exception is small or large. However, if the person excepts the entire amount (e.g., 'I owe you a thousand except a thousand'), the exception is void and the full iqrar stands, because an exception that leaves nothing is effectively a retraction (ruju'). This principle is analogized to divorce. The commentary then delves into a dispute among scholars regarding the permissibility of excepting the majority (istithna al-akthar). Some grammarians and Imams (Zufar, Ahmad, Ibn Durustawayh, and a narration from Abu Yusuf) hold that excepting the majority is invalid because it is not customary in Arabic speech. However, the majority of scholars (including the Hanafi school) consider it valid, citing Quranic verses where Allah excepts a large portion (e.g., in Surah al-Muzzammil, Allah commands standing except a little, then allows reducing to half or adding, which implies exception of a majority). The stronger evidence is from Surah al-Hijr: 'I will surely mislead them all, except Your chosen servants among them' where the excepted are few (mukhlisin) and the rest are many (ghawin). Thus, exception of the majority is affirmed linguistically and legally.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna): Exception: a statement that excludes part of what is included in a previous general statement, e.g., 'I owe you a thousand except one hundred'.
مستثنى منه (mustathna minhu): The general term from which the exception is made (e.g., 'a thousand' in the example).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'I owe you 500 except 400' (immediately after)
B) 'I owe you 500 except 500'
C) 'I owe you 500' (then after a pause) 'except 100'
D) 'I owe you 500 except 600'

Key Takeaway
A connected exception in iqrar is valid and binds only the remainder; exception of the majority is valid, supported by Quranic evidence, and is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
