intermediate
12 min
Precedence of Debts with Known Causes and Restrictions on Acknowledgment and Payment
States that debts with known causes take precedence and restricts preferential payment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for precedence of debts with known causes and apply the prohibition against a sick person's preferential payment to creditors.

Core Idea
Debts with known causes are trusted; no preferential payment allowed during illness.

When a person is terminally ill, questions of debt distribution become delicate. The Hanafi school gives certain debts priority—those whose causes are known and witnessed, like the price of a purchase or proper dowry. But not all debts are treated equally; the sick person cannot play favorites with creditors. This lesson unpacks the rationale and the specific rulings, including an exception for debts incurred during the illness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of debts
Distinguish between debts with known causes (ma'rufat al-asbab) and other debts. The passage gives examples: price of a purchase, compensation for destroyed property, proper dower.
Known cause means the reason for the debt is witnessed and beyond suspicion.
2
Understand the rationale for precedence
The text states that debts with known causes are given precedence because there is no suspicion (tuhmah) in their establishment; what is witnessed cannot be rejected.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on absence of suspicion.
3
Apply the rule on acknowledgment of a specific asset
If a sick person acknowledges a specific asset (ayn) in his possession as belonging to another, it is invalid against health-time creditors because their right has already attached to that asset.
This is the Hanafi position; the three other imams hold it valid.
4
Apply the prohibition of preferential payment
The sick person cannot pay some creditors and ignore others, as this nullifies the rights of the remaining creditors. This applies equally to health-time and illness-time creditors.
There is an exception for debts incurred during the illness itself (e.g., a loan taken or a purchase made during illness) if proven by evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معلومة الاسباب دیون کے مقدم ہونے کی وجہ

وَإِنَّمَا تَقَدَّمَ الْمَعْرُوفَةَ الْأَسْبَابِ لاَنَّهُ لَا تُهُمَةَ فِي تُبُوتِهَا إِذَ الْمُعَايِنُ لَا مَرَدَّ لَهُ وَذَالِكَ مِثْلَ بَدَلَ مَالٍ مَلِكَهُ أَوِ اسْتَهْلَكَهُ وَعُلِمَ وَجُوْبُهُ بِغَيْرِ إِقْرَارِهِ أَوْ تَزَوَّجَ اِمْرَأَةٌ بِمَهْرٍ مِثْلِهَا وَهَذَا الدَّيْنُ مِثْلَ دَيْنِ الصَّحَةِ لَا يُقَدَّمُ أَحَدُهُمَا عَلَى الْآخَرِ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا وَلَوْ أَقَرَّ بِعَيْنِ فِي يَدِهِ لِأَخَرَ لَمْ يَصِحُ فِي حَقِّ غُرَمَاءِ الصَّحَةِ لِتَعَلَّقِ حَقِّهِمْ بِهِ وَلَا يَجُوزُ لِلْمَرِيضِ أَنْ يَقْضِيَ دَيْنَ بَعْضُ الْغُرَمَاءِ دُونَ الْبَعْضِ لَانَّ فِي إِيْتَارِ الْبَعْضِ إِبْطَالُ حَقِّ الْبَاقِينَ وَغُرَمَاءُ الصّحَةِ وَالْمَرَضِ فِى ذَالِكَ سَوَاءٌ إِلَّا إِذَا قَضَى مَا اسْتَقْرَضَ فِي مَرَضِهِ أَوْ نَقَدَ ثَمَنَ مَا اشْتَرَى فِي مَرِضِهِ وَقَدْ عُلِمَ بِالْبَيِّنَةِ

ترجمہ اور معروف اسباب والے قرضے مقدم اس لئے کئے جائیں گے کہ ان کے ثبوت میں کوئی تہمت نہیں۔ کیونکہ آنکھوں دیکھی چیز کے رد کی گنجائش نہیں۔ اور یہ مشل اس مال کے بدل کے ہے۔ جس کا وہ مالک ہو یا تلف کیا اور اس کا وجوب اقرار کے علاوہ سے معلوم ہو گیا یا اس نے کسی عورت سے اس کے مہر مثل کے عوض نکاح کیا۔ یہ قرضہ بھی دین صحت کے مثل ہے۔ کوئی ایک دوسرے پر مقدم نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ بدلیل سابق اگر اقرار کیا بیمار نے دوسرے کے لئے ایسے مال عین کا جو اس کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ تو صحیح نہ ہو گا۔ صحت کے قرض خواہوں کے حق میں۔ کیونکہ ان کا حق اس مال سے وابستہ ہو چکا اور جائز نہیں مریض کے لئے بعض قرض خواہوں کا قرض چکانا ۔ کیونکہ بعض کو ترجیح دینے میں باقی قرض خواہوں کا حق باطل کرنا ہے اور اس میں تندرستی و بیماری کے قرض خواہ برابر ہیں۔ مگر یہ کہ ایسا قرض چکائے جو اس نے حالت مرض میں کیا ہے یا اس کے دار چکائے جو اس نے حالت مرض میں خریدی ہے۔ اور بعینہ سے معلوم ہوگئی ہے۔

تشریح قوله وانما تقدم پھر حالت مرض کے ایسے قرضے جن کے اسباب معلوم ہیں مثلا کسی طبیع کا شمن بوجہ بیچ کے یا کسی عورت کا مہر بوجہ ماج کے لازم آیا ہے تو ان کے مقدم ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ان کے ثبوت میں تہمت کا کوئی امکان نہیں۔ کیونکہ مشاہد چیز کے رد کی گنجائش نہیں ہوتی۔ اس کی مثال یہ ہے کہ قرضہ ایسے مال کی وجہ سے لازم آیا جو مال اس نے اپنی ملک میں لیا ہے یا اس نے کسی کا مال تلف کیا اور اس کا وجوب اقرار کے علاوہ معائنہ یا گواہی کی دلیل سے معلوم ہو گیا یا اس نے کسی عورت سے اس کے مہر مثل پر نکاح کیا تو ایسے قرضے قرضہ صحت کے برابر ہیں۔ کسی ایک کو دوسرے پر ترجیح نہیں کیونکہ ان کے ثبوت میں کوئی تہمت نہیں ہے۔

قوله ولواقربعين .. مریض کے قبضہ میں کوئی معین مال ہے جس کی بابت اس نے اقرار کیا کہ یہ لا شخص کا ہے تو خرما بحت کے حق میں اس کا یہ اقرار صحیح نہیں۔ (ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک صحیح ہے) کیونکہ اس مال کے ساتھ ان کا حق وابستہ ہو چکا ہے۔

قوله ولا يجوز للمريض مریض مذکور کے لئے یہ بات جائز نہیں کہ وہ بعض غرماء کا قرضہ ادا کرے اور بعض کا ادانہ کرے۔ کیونکہ اس طرح کرنے میں دوسروں کی حق تلفی ہے۔ خواہ غرماء صحت ہوں یا غرماء مرض ہوں۔ ہاں اگر اس نے بحالت مرض وہ قرض چکا یا جو حالت مرض ہی
The reason for giving precedence to debts with known causes: And debts with known causes are given precedence only because there is no suspicion in their establishment, because what is witnessed cannot be rejected. That is like the compensation for property he owned or destroyed and its obligation is known without his acknowledgment, or he married a woman with her proper dower. This debt is like a health-time debt; neither is given precedence over the other, as we explained. And if he acknowledges a specific asset in his hand for another, it is not valid in respect to health-time creditors, because their right has attached to it. And it is not permissible for the sick person to pay the debt of some creditors without others, because giving preference to some involves nullifying the right of the remaining. And health-time and illness-time creditors are equal in this, except if he pays what he borrowed during his illness, or pays the price of what he bought during his illness, and it is known by evidence. Translation: Debts with known causes will be given precedence because there is no suspicion in their proof, because an observed thing cannot be rejected. This is like the compensation for property which he owned or destroyed, and its obligation is known without his acknowledgment, or he married a woman with her proper dower. This debt is like a health-time debt; neither is given precedence over the other. By the previous proof, if a sick person acknowledges a specific asset in his possession for another, it will not be valid in respect to health-time creditors, because their right has attached to it. And it is not permissible for the sick person to pay the debt of some creditors without others, because giving preference to some involves nullifying the right of the remaining. And health-time and illness-time creditors are equal in this, except if he pays what he borrowed during his illness, or pays the price of what he bought during his illness, and it is known by evidence. Explanation: The statement 'and only debts with known causes are given precedence' then in the state of illness, debts whose causes are known, such as a payment for a purchase or a woman's dower due to marriage, the reason for their precedence is that there is no possibility of suspicion in their proof, because an observed thing cannot be rejected. Examples: a debt arising from property he took into his ownership, or he destroyed someone's property, and its obligation is known through inspection or testimony without acknowledgment, or he married a woman with her proper dower. Such debts are equal to health-time debts; none is given precedence over another because there is no suspicion in their proof. His statement 'and if he acknowledges...' means if the sick person has a specific asset in his possession and he acknowledges that it belongs to another person, this acknowledgment is not valid against health-time creditors (according to the three imams it is valid) because their right has attached to that asset. His statement 'and it is not permissible for the sick person...' means it is not permissible for the mentioned sick person to pay the debt of some creditors and not others, because doing so harms the rights of others, whether the creditors are from health or illness time. Yes, if during his illness he pays a debt that he incurred during illness itself.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage outlines rules regarding debts in terminal illness. It first explains that debts with known causes (ma'rufat al-asbab), such as a price for a purchase or proper dowry, are given precedence over other debts because their existence is known without suspicion. These debts are treated like health-time debts—none outranks another. Then it addresses two prohibitions: First, if a sick person acknowledges a specific asset in his possession as belonging to someone else, this acknowledgment is invalid against health-time creditors (with a note that the three imams hold it valid). The reason is that creditors' rights have attached to that asset. Second, a sick person cannot pay some creditors while excluding others, as this prejudices the excluded ones. An exception is made for debts incurred during the illness itself, such as a loan taken during illness or the price of goods bought during illness, if proven. The commentary explains each part, giving examples and clarifying the underlying rationale (lack of suspicion).

Key Terms
معروفة الاسباب (ma'rufat al-asbab): Debts whose causes are known and proven without suspicion, such as price of a purchase or proper dowry.
غرماء (ghurama'): Creditors; those to whom the deceased owes debts.
عين ('ayn): A specific, tangible asset (as opposed to debt or obligation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a sick person acknowledges that a specific asset in his possession belongs to a friend, what is the ruling regarding health-time creditors?
A) The acknowledgment is valid and the friend takes the asset.
B) The acknowledgment is invalid against health-time creditors.
C) The acknowledgment is valid only if the sick person was healthy at the time.
D) The acknowledgment is valid only if the friend is a relative.

Key Takeaway
Debts with known causes are given precedence over others, and a sick person cannot pay some creditors preferentially—all are equal, except for debts incurred during the illness itself.
